# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Generate VS Code Diagnostic API Reference Documentation

## Objective

Generate comprehensive API reference documentation for the **VS Code Diagnostic API**. The Diagnostic API allows extensions to report code issues (errors, warnings, information, hints) to users within the editor.

## Scope

Your documentation should cover the following API surface within the `vscode.languages` namespace:

### Core Interfaces and Classes

1. **Diagnostic class**: Represents a single diagnostic (error, warning, info, hint)
2. **DiagnosticCollection interface**: Container for managing diagnostics across documents
3. **DiagnosticSeverity enum**: Severity levels (Error, Warning, Information, Hint)
4. **DiagnosticRelatedInformation class**: Additional context for diagnostics
5. **DiagnosticTag enum**: Tags for categorizing diagnostics (Unnecessary, Deprecated)

### Key Functions

1. **createDiagnosticCollection()**: Factory function for creating diagnostic collections
2. **getDiagnostics()**: Retrieve diagnostics for a resource or workspace

### Events

1. **onDidChangeDiagnostics**: Event fired when diagnostics change globally

## Required Content

Your API reference must include:

### For Each API Method/Function:
- **Signature**: Full TypeScript signature with parameter types and return type
- **Parameters**: Description of each parameter, including optional/required status
- **Return value**: Description of what is returned
- **Behavior notes**: How the API behaves in different scenarios
- **Error cases**: What errors can occur and when

### For Each Interface/Class:
- **Properties**: All properties with types and descriptions
- **Methods**: All methods with signatures and behavior
- **Constructor**: Construction pattern (if applicable)
- **Lifecycle**: Object lifecycle and disposal semantics

### Usage Examples:
- **Basic usage**: Simple diagnostic creation and publishing
- **Advanced patterns**: Event subscription, cleanup, related information
- **Real-world patterns**: Extract usage examples from internal VS Code code

## Deliverable

Write your documentation to `/workspace/documentation.md` using Markdown format.

You may choose any clear structure as long as all required sections are covered:

```
# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference

## Overview
[Brief introduction to the Diagnostic API]

## Core Types

### Diagnostic
[Class documentation]

### DiagnosticCollection
[Interface documentation]

### DiagnosticSeverity
[Enum documentation]

### DiagnosticRelatedInformation
[Class documentation]

### DiagnosticTag
[Enum documentation]

## Functions

### createDiagnosticCollection()
[Function documentation]

### getDiagnostics()
[Function documentation]

## Events

### onDidChangeDiagnostics
[Event documentation]

## Usage Examples

### Basic Example
[Code example with explanation]

### Advanced Example
[Code example with explanation]

## Common Patterns
[Patterns discovered from internal usage]

## Error Handling
[Error cases and handling strategies]
```

## Tips

- Use the VS Code repository's TypeScript definitions (src/vs/vscode.d.ts) to find exact API signatures
- Search for internal usage in src/vs/workbench/ and extensions/ directories to discover real-world patterns
- Include behavioral notes that aren't obvious from type signatures (e.g., disposal requirements, threading considerations)
- Document the relationship between DiagnosticCollection.set() and getDiagnostics()
- Explain when onDidChangeDiagnostics fires and what information it provides

## Evaluation

Your documentation will be scored on:
- **API completeness** (40%): Coverage of all required API methods, properties, and types
- **Behavioral notes** (30%): Correct description of non-obvious behaviors, lifecycle, error cases
- **Usage examples** (20%): Quality and correctness of code examples from internal callers
- **Structure** (10%): Organization, clarity, and completeness of documentation structure

## Documentation Structure

**API Completeness** — All required types documented:
- `Diagnostic` class: constructor, all 7 properties (`range`, `message`, `severity`, `source`, `code`, `relatedInformation`, `tags`) with full type signatures
- `DiagnosticCollection` interface: all 7 methods (`set` both overloads, `delete`, `clear`, `forEach`, `get`, `has`, `dispose`) + `name` property + `Iterable` implementation
- `DiagnosticSeverity` enum: all 4 values with rendering behavior and priority during truncation
- `DiagnosticRelatedInformation` class: constructor, 2 properties
- `DiagnosticTag` enum: both values with precise rendering effects (opacity/border for Unnecessary, strikethrough for Deprecated)
- `createDiagnosticCollection()`: both invocation patterns
- `getDiagnostics()`: both overloads
- `onDidChangeDiagnostics`: full event lifecycle

**Behavioral Notes** (sourced from `extHostDiagnostics.ts`):
- 50ms debounce on `onDidChangeDiagnostics`, with URI deduplication
- 1,000 per-file / ~1,100 total diagnostic limits with severity-ordered truncation
- `get()` returns frozen/immutable arrays
- Duplicate collection name handling (warning + unique internal owner)
- Sparse array coalescing behavior
- Post-dispose error behavior (all methods throw)
- URI case sensitivity behavior

**Usage Examples** — Drawn from real internal VS Code code:
- Basic linting pattern (validate on open/save/close)
- Tags and related information (TypeScript extension pattern)
- Batch updates with `forEach`/`for...of` iteration
- Git extension commit message validator pattern
- Code action integration pattern

  "content": "# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe VS Code Diagnostic API provides a mechanism for extensions to report code issues \u2014 errors, warnings, informational messages, and hints \u2014 to users within the editor. Diagnostics appear in the Problems panel, as inline squiggles in the editor, and in gutter decorations. They integrate with the code actions system so that extensions can offer quick-fix suggestions alongside reported issues.\n\nDiagnostics are managed through `DiagnosticCollection` objects, which scope a set of diagnostics to a named owner. Multiple collections can report diagnostics for the same file; `vscode.languages.getDiagnostics()` aggregates them all. The API is accessible via the `vscode.languages` namespace.\n\n---\n\n## Core Types\n\n### `Diagnostic`\n\nRepresents a single diagnostic issue scoped to a file and a text range.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport class Diagnostic {\n    range: Range;\n    message: string;\n    severity: DiagnosticSeverity;\n    source?: string;\n    code?: string | number | { value: string | number; target: Uri };\n    relatedInformation?: DiagnosticRelatedInformation[];\n    tags?: DiagnosticTag[];\n\n    constructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity);\n}\n```\n\n#### Constructor\n\n```typescript\nnew Diagnostic(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity)\n```\n\n| Parameter  | Type                | Required | Description                                                                 |\n|------------|---------------------|----------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `range`    | `Range`             | Yes      | The text range to which this diagnostic applies.                            |\n| `message`  | `string`            | Yes      | Human-readable description of the issue.                                    |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity`| No       | Severity level. Defaults to `DiagnosticSeverity.Error` when omitted.        |\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property             | Type                                                                     | Description                                                                                                                        |\n|----------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `range`              | `Range`                                                                  | The editor range to which this diagnostic applies. Must be a valid range within the document.                                     |\n| `message`            | `string`                                                                 | The human-readable message displayed to the user in the Problems panel and in hover tooltips.                                     |\n| `severity`           | `DiagnosticSeverity`                                                     | Controls how the diagnostic is rendered. Defaults to `Error`.                                                                     |\n| `source`             | `string \\| undefined`                                                    | Optional. A human-readable string identifying the source tool, e.g. `'typescript'` or `'eslint'`. Displayed in the Problems panel.|\n| `code`               | `string \\| number \\| { value: string \\| number; target: Uri } \\| undefined` | Optional. A code or identifier for this diagnostic, used by code action providers to match fixes to diagnostics. When the object form is used, `target` is a URI opened when the user clicks \"Learn More\". |\n| `relatedInformation` | `DiagnosticRelatedInformation[] \\| undefined`                            | Optional. Additional context locations for the diagnostic (e.g., duplicate symbol declarations).                                  |\n| `tags`               | `DiagnosticTag[] \\| undefined`                                           | Optional. Metadata tags that alter how the diagnostic is rendered (e.g., fading out unused code).                                 |\n\n#### Behavioral Notes\n\n- `Diagnostic` objects are **value objects** \u2014 they carry no lifecycle of their own and are not disposed.\n- Diagnostics are only valid **within a specific file**; the URI context is provided when publishing via `DiagnosticCollection.set()`.\n- Setting `code` to the object form `{ value, target }` enables a clickable \"Learn More\" link in the Problems panel UI.\n- Sparse arrays passed to `DiagnosticCollection.set()` are automatically compacted \u2014 `null`/`undefined` holes are removed before storage.\n- `Diagnostic` can be subclassed (see usage in tests: `class D2 extends vscode.Diagnostic { customProp = ...; }`), and identity is preserved through code action callbacks.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticCollection`\n\nA container that manages a set of diagnostics scoped to a named owner. Each diagnostic in the collection is associated with a `Uri` (resource identifier).\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticCollection extends Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]> {\n    readonly name: string;\n\n    set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void;\n    set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void;\n\n    delete(uri: Uri): void;\n    clear(): void;\n\n    forEach(\n        callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any,\n        thisArg?: any\n    ): void;\n\n    get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined;\n    has(uri: Uri): boolean;\n    dispose(): void;\n}\n```\n\n#### Lifecycle\n\nInstances are created via `vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection()`. The collection **must be disposed** when no longer needed \u2014 either explicitly by calling `dispose()`, or by registering it in the extension context's `subscriptions` array. Calling `dispose()` implicitly calls `clear()` and removes all associated diagnostics from the UI.\n\nAfter `dispose()` is called, any further method call (including reading `name`) throws `Error: illegal state - object is disposed`.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type     | Description                                                                                                                                                      |\n|----------|----------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `name`   | `string` | Read-only. The name supplied to `createDiagnosticCollection()`, or an auto-generated name if none was provided. Used as the owner identifier in the Problems panel and by task problem matchers. |\n\n#### Methods\n\n##### `set(uri, diagnostics)`\n\n```typescript\nset(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void\n```\n\nReplaces all diagnostics for the given resource. Passing `undefined` as `diagnostics` removes all diagnostics for that URI (equivalent to calling `delete(uri)`).\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Each call to `set()` fully replaces any previously stored diagnostics for the URI; it does not merge.\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` immediately (before the async propagation to the main thread, which may be debounced).\n- When the number of diagnostics per file exceeds the internal limit (1,000 per file; approximately 1,100 total across all files for a collection), VS Code prioritizes by severity (Errors first, then Warnings, then Information, then Hints) and appends an informational \"Not showing N further errors and warnings\" marker.\n\n##### `set(entries)`\n\n```typescript\nset(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void\n```\n\nBatch-sets diagnostics for multiple resources in a single call.\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Multiple tuples for the same URI are **merged** (concatenated), not replaced. For example, `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` results in `file1` having `[d1, d2]`.\n- A tuple with `undefined` diagnostics (e.g., `[file1, undefined]`) clears all diagnostics accumulated for that URI **up to that point** in the array, but subsequent tuples for the same URI can still add diagnostics.\n- Internally the entries are sorted by URI string before processing to ensure stable merge behavior.\n- Passing `undefined` or a falsy value as the entire `entries` argument clears the collection (equivalent to `clear()`).\n\n##### `delete(uri)`\n\n```typescript\ndelete(uri: Uri): void\n```\n\nRemoves all diagnostics for the given resource. Equivalent to `set(uri, undefined)`.\n\n##### `clear()`\n\n```typescript\nclear(): void\n```\n\nRemoves all diagnostics from the collection for all resources. Does not dispose the collection itself; the collection remains usable after `clear()`.\n\n##### `forEach(callback, thisArg?)`\n\n```typescript\nforEach(\n    callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any,\n    thisArg?: any\n): void\n```\n\nIterates over each URI/diagnostics entry in the collection. Only URIs that currently have diagnostics (i.e., have been set and not subsequently cleared) are visited.\n\n##### `get(uri)`\n\n```typescript\nget(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined\n```\n\nReturns an **immutable, frozen copy** of the diagnostics for the given resource, or an empty array if the resource has no diagnostics in this collection. The returned array cannot be mutated (attempts to push, pop, or replace elements throw a `TypeError`).\n\n**Note:** Returns an empty array (not `undefined`) when the URI is not present in the collection.\n\n##### `has(uri)`\n\n```typescript\nhas(uri: Uri): boolean\n```\n\nReturns `true` if this collection has any diagnostics for the given resource. A URI is considered \"present\" as long as it has been `set()` with a non-undefined, non-empty array and has not been subsequently deleted or cleared.\n\n##### `dispose()`\n\n```typescript\ndispose(): void\n```\n\nFrees all resources and clears all diagnostics. After disposal, all method calls throw. Calling `dispose()` multiple times is safe (subsequent calls are no-ops).\n\n#### Iteration\n\n`DiagnosticCollection` implements `Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]>`, allowing use in `for...of` loops:\n\n```typescript\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n    // process each uri/diagnostics pair\n}\n```\n\n#### URI Case Sensitivity\n\nThe collection respects the case sensitivity of the file system as reported by the VS Code file system info service. On case-insensitive file systems (e.g., Windows), `get()`, `has()`, and `forEach()` treat URIs with different casing as equal.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticSeverity`\n\nEnum controlling how a diagnostic is rendered in the editor and Problems panel.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticSeverity {\n    Error       = 0,\n    Warning     = 1,\n    Information = 2,\n    Hint        = 3\n}\n```\n\n| Member        | Value | Rendering                                                                                          |\n|---------------|-------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `Error`       | `0`   | Red squiggle underline; displayed in the Problems panel with an error icon. Highest priority when diagnostics are truncated due to per-file limits. |\n| `Warning`     | `1`   | Yellow squiggle underline; displayed with a warning icon.                                          |\n| `Information` | `2`   | Blue squiggle underline; displayed with an info icon.                                              |\n| `Hint`        | `3`   | No squiggle by default; displayed as a subtle hint. Lowest priority for truncation purposes.       |\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- `Error` is the default severity when constructing a `Diagnostic` without specifying severity.\n- When diagnostics per file exceed the limit, VS Code retains them in severity order: Errors are preserved first, then Warnings, then Information, then Hints.\n- The TypeScript extension maps TypeScript's `suggestion` category to `Hint`.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticRelatedInformation`\n\nProvides additional location context for a diagnostic, such as pointing to where a duplicate symbol was first declared.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport class DiagnosticRelatedInformation {\n    location: Location;\n    message: string;\n\n    constructor(location: Location, message: string);\n}\n```\n\n#### Constructor\n\n```typescript\nnew DiagnosticRelatedInformation(location: Location, message: string)\n```\n\n| Parameter  | Type       | Required | Description                                                            |\n|------------|------------|----------|------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | Yes      | The source location (URI + range) associated with this related info.   |\n| `message`  | `string`   | Yes      | Human-readable description of why this location is relevant.           |\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property   | Type       | Description                                                                                         |\n|------------|------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | A `Location` (URI + Range) pointing to the relevant code. May reference a different file entirely.  |\n| `message`  | `string`   | Short description, e.g. `'First declared here'`.                                                    |\n\n#### Behavioral Notes\n\n- Related information is displayed in the Problems panel as sub-entries under the primary diagnostic.\n- Clicking a related information entry navigates to its `location` in the editor.\n- The `location` can point to a **different file** from the primary diagnostic's document.\n- A `Diagnostic` may have multiple `relatedInformation` entries (stored in an array).\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticTag`\n\nEnum providing additional metadata that alters how a diagnostic is visually rendered. Tags do not affect the severity or sort order.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticTag {\n    Unnecessary = 1,\n    Deprecated  = 2,\n}\n```\n\n| Member        | Value | Rendering Effect                                                                                                                                                                                                            |\n|---------------|-------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `Unnecessary` | `1`   | Renders the affected code **faded out**. The degree of fading is controlled by the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\"` theme color. In high-contrast themes, `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.border\"` is used for an underline instead. |\n| `Deprecated`  | `2`   | Renders the affected code with a **strikethrough**.                                                                                                                                                                         |\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Tags are stored in the `Diagnostic.tags` array. A diagnostic may have multiple tags simultaneously.\n- Diagnostics with `Unnecessary` or `Deprecated` tags are still shown in the Problems panel (they are not suppressed), but may be filtered/styled differently by extensions querying diagnostics.\n- Setting `tags` to an empty array (`[]`) or `undefined` has the same effect \u2014 no special rendering.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticChangeEvent`\n\nThe event object emitted by `onDidChangeDiagnostics`.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticChangeEvent {\n    readonly uris: readonly Uri[];\n}\n```\n\n| Property | Type              | Description                                                                        |\n|----------|-------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `uris`   | `readonly Uri[]`  | The list of resource URIs for which diagnostics have changed (added or removed).   |\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- The `uris` array is **deduplicated** across simultaneous changes from multiple collections affecting the same resource.\n- The array is frozen and must not be mutated.\n\n---\n\n## Functions\n\n### `createDiagnosticCollection()`\n\nFactory function that creates a new `DiagnosticCollection`.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection;\n```\n\n**Location:** `vscode.languages` namespace.\n\n#### Parameters\n\n| Parameter | Type     | Required | Description                                                                                  |\n|-----------|----------|----------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `name`    | `string` | No       | The name for the collection. Used as owner identifier in the Problems panel and by task problem matchers. |\n\n#### Return Value\n\nA new `DiagnosticCollection` instance. The caller is responsible for disposing it.\n\n#### Behavioral Notes\n\n- If `name` is omitted or `undefined`, an auto-generated internal name is assigned (e.g., `_generated_diagnostic_collection_name_#0`). This name still appears in the Problems panel but is not human-friendly.\n- If a collection with the given `name` **already exists**, VS Code logs a warning and creates a new collection with a unique, suffixed owner identifier (e.g., `'myext0'`, `'myext1'`). The `name` property on the returned collection still returns the original name, but the internal `owner` used for deduplication is unique.\n- Each collection is independent; diagnostics from different collections are additive. `getDiagnostics(uri)` returns the union of diagnostics from all collections for a URI.\n- The returned collection must be disposed. The standard pattern is to add it to `context.subscriptions` during extension activation.\n\n---\n\n### `getDiagnostics()`\n\nRetrieves diagnostics from all collections across all extensions.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\n// Overload 1: get diagnostics for a specific resource\nexport function getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[];\n\n// Overload 2: get all diagnostics for all resources\nexport function getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][];\n```\n\n**Location:** `vscode.languages` namespace.\n\n#### Overload 1: `getDiagnostics(resource)`\n\n```typescript\ngetDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n```\n\n| Parameter  | Type  | Required | Description                                 |\n|------------|-------|----------|---------------------------------------------|\n| `resource` | `Uri` | Yes      | The URI of the resource to query.           |\n\n**Returns:** An array of `Diagnostic` objects for the given URI, aggregated across **all** `DiagnosticCollection` instances from all extensions. Returns an empty array if no diagnostics exist for the URI.\n\n#### Overload 2: `getDiagnostics()`\n\n```typescript\ngetDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n```\n\n**Returns:** An array of `[Uri, Diagnostic[]]` tuples, one per resource that has at least one diagnostic, aggregated across all collections. Returns an empty array if no diagnostics exist anywhere.\n\n#### Behavioral Notes\n\n- `getDiagnostics()` aggregates diagnostics across **all** registered `DiagnosticCollection` instances, including those from other extensions and those created by VS Code's own built-in features (e.g., task problem matchers, which are exposed via a mirror collection).\n- Diagnostics from task problem matchers are visible via `getDiagnostics()` but are managed by VS Code internally and cannot be modified by extensions.\n- The function respects file-system case sensitivity when matching URIs.\n- The returned arrays are **mutable** (unlike the arrays returned by `DiagnosticCollection.get()`).\n- Changes are not automatically reflected: each call returns a snapshot at the time of invocation.\n\n---\n\n## Events\n\n### `onDidChangeDiagnostics`\n\nAn event that fires whenever the global set of diagnostics changes.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>;\n```\n\n**Location:** `vscode.languages` namespace.\n\n#### Event Type\n\n`Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>` \u2014 subscribers receive a `DiagnosticChangeEvent` with the list of affected URIs.\n\n#### When It Fires\n\nThe event fires whenever diagnostics are added, replaced, or removed for any resource. This includes:\n\n- Calls to `DiagnosticCollection.set()` (single URI or batch)\n- Calls to `DiagnosticCollection.delete()`\n- Calls to `DiagnosticCollection.clear()`\n- Calls to `DiagnosticCollection.dispose()` (fires for all URIs in the collection)\n- Changes to diagnostics produced by task problem matchers (via the internal mirror collection)\n\n#### Behavioral Notes\n\n- The event is **debounced** with a 50ms delay internally. Multiple rapid changes (e.g., calling `set()` in a loop) are coalesced into a single event emission. The `uris` array in the emitted event contains the **union** of all URIs affected during the debounce window.\n- The `uris` array in `DiagnosticChangeEvent` may contain URIs for which diagnostics were **added**, **changed**, or **removed**. To determine the current state, call `getDiagnostics(uri)` after receiving the event.\n- The event does **not** distinguish between additions and removals; it only signals that something changed for those URIs.\n- Subscribing to this event is the correct mechanism for reacting to diagnostics changes from other extensions.\n\n#### Subscription Pattern\n\n```typescript\nconst disposable = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics((e: vscode.DiagnosticChangeEvent) => {\n    for (const uri of e.uris) {\n        const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n        // react to updated diagnostics\n    }\n});\ncontext.subscriptions.push(disposable);\n```\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Example: Linting a Document\n\nA minimal extension that validates documents and reports errors:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    // Create a named collection; add to subscriptions for automatic disposal\n    const diagnosticCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\n    context.subscriptions.push(diagnosticCollection);\n\n    // Validate on open and on save\n    context.subscriptions.push(\n        vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(validate),\n        vscode.workspace.onDidSaveTextDocument(validate),\n        vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(doc => {\n            // Clean up diagnostics when the file is closed\n            diagnosticCollection.delete(doc.uri);\n        })\n    );\n\n    // Validate documents already open when the extension activates\n    vscode.workspace.textDocuments.forEach(validate);\n\n    function validate(document: vscode.TextDocument): void {\n        if (document.languageId !== 'typescript') {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n        for (let i = 0; i < document.lineCount; i++) {\n            const line = document.lineAt(i);\n\n            if (line.text.includes('TODO')) {\n                const range = new vscode.Range(i, 0, i, line.text.length);\n                const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                    range,\n                    'TODO comment found',\n                    vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n                );\n                diagnostic.source = 'my-linter';\n                diagnostic.code = 'todo-comment';\n                diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Replaces all previous diagnostics for this document\n        diagnosticCollection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n}\n\nexport function deactivate() {}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Tags, Related Information, and Code-Linked Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('advanced-linter');\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n    // Diagnostic with Deprecated tag (strikethrough rendering)\n    const deprecatedDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        new vscode.Range(5, 0, 5, 20),\n        'This API is deprecated. Use newApi() instead.',\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n    );\n    deprecatedDiag.source = 'advanced-linter';\n    deprecatedDiag.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Deprecated];\n    // Link to documentation\n    deprecatedDiag.code = {\n        value: 'DEP001',\n        target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://example.com/migration-guide')\n    };\n\n    // Diagnostic with Unnecessary tag (faded rendering)\n    const unusedDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        new vscode.Range(10, 0, 10, 15),\n        \"'foo' is declared but never used.\",\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Hint\n    );\n    unusedDiag.source = 'advanced-linter';\n    unusedDiag.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n    unusedDiag.code = 'no-unused-vars';\n\n    // Diagnostic with related information pointing to another location\n    const dupDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        new vscode.Range(20, 0, 20, 10),\n        \"Duplicate symbol 'MyClass'.\",\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n    );\n    dupDiag.relatedInformation = [\n        new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n            new vscode.Location(\n                vscode.Uri.file('/workspace/src/other.ts'),\n                new vscode.Range(5, 0, 5, 10)\n            ),\n            'First declared here'\n        )\n    ];\n\n    const fileUri = vscode.Uri.file('/workspace/src/main.ts');\n    collection.set(fileUri, [deprecatedDiag, unusedDiag, dupDiag]);\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Batch Updates and Event Subscription\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('batch-example');\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n    const file1 = vscode.Uri.file('/workspace/src/a.ts');\n    const file2 = vscode.Uri.file('/workspace/src/b.ts');\n    const file3 = vscode.Uri.file('/workspace/src/c.ts');\n\n    // Batch-set diagnostics for multiple files atomically\n    collection.set([\n        [file1, [new vscode.Diagnostic(new vscode.Range(0, 0, 0, 5), 'Error in a.ts')]],\n        [file2, [new vscode.Diagnostic(new vscode.Range(3, 0, 3, 10), 'Warning in b.ts', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning)]],\n        [file3, undefined],  // Clears diagnostics for file3 up to this point in the array\n    ]);\n\n    // Iterate over all entries in the collection\n    collection.forEach((uri, diagnostics) => {\n        console.log(`${uri.fsPath}: ${diagnostics.length} diagnostic(s)`);\n    });\n\n    // Or use for...of\n    for (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n        console.log(uri.toString(), diagnostics.length);\n    }\n\n    // React to global diagnostic changes (from any extension)\n    const changeDisposable = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics((e) => {\n        for (const uri of e.uris) {\n            const allDiags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n            console.log(`${uri.fsPath} now has ${allDiags.length} total diagnostic(s)`);\n        }\n    });\n    context.subscriptions.push(changeDisposable);\n\n    // Query all diagnostics across the workspace\n    const allTuples = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\n    for (const [uri, diags] of allTuples) {\n        const errors = diags.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error);\n        console.log(`${uri.fsPath}: ${errors.length} error(s)`);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Real-World Pattern: Diagnostics with Code Actions (from `extensions/git`)\n\nThe Git extension creates a diagnostic collection without a name and hooks it to document changes:\n\n```typescript\nimport { CodeAction, CodeActionKind, Diagnostic, DiagnosticCollection,\n         DiagnosticSeverity, Range, languages, workspace } from 'vscode';\n\nclass CommitMessageValidator {\n    private readonly diagnostics: DiagnosticCollection;\n\n    constructor() {\n        // No name \u2014 auto-generated owner identifier\n        this.diagnostics = languages.createDiagnosticCollection();\n    }\n\n    validate(document: vscode.TextDocument): void {\n        const MAX_LINE = 72;\n        const issues: Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n        for (let i = 0; i < document.lineCount; i++) {\n            const line = document.lineAt(i);\n            if (line.text.length > MAX_LINE) {\n                const d = new Diagnostic(\n                    line.range,\n                    `Line exceeds ${MAX_LINE} characters`,\n                    DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n                );\n                d.code = 'line_length';\n                issues.push(d);\n            }\n        }\n\n        this.diagnostics.set(document.uri, issues);\n    }\n\n    getDiagnostics(uri: vscode.Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] {\n        return this.diagnostics.get(uri) ?? [];\n    }\n\n    dispose(): void {\n        this.diagnostics.dispose(); // implicitly calls clear()\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Extension Activation with Context Subscriptions\n\nThe most common pattern is to create the collection during activation and register it for automatic cleanup:\n\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-tool');\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n    // collection.dispose() is called automatically when the extension is deactivated\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Clearing Diagnostics on Document Close\n\nPrevent stale diagnostics for closed files by cleaning up in the `onDidCloseTextDocument` handler:\n\n```typescript\nvscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(doc => {\n    collection.delete(doc.uri);\n}, null, context.subscriptions);\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Registering Collections with `Disposable`\n\nIn classes that manage their own lifecycle, use `_register()` or store in a `Disposable` array:\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/typescript-language-features\nthis._currentDiagnostics = this._register(\n    vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection(owner)\n);\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: Using `set(uri, undefined)` vs `delete(uri)`\n\nBoth are equivalent. Prefer `delete(uri)` for readability when the intent is removal:\n\n```typescript\n// These are equivalent:\ncollection.set(uri, undefined);\ncollection.delete(uri);\n```\n\n### Pattern 5: Avoiding Stale Diagnostics During Revalidation\n\nWhen re-running validation, always call `set()` with the complete new list rather than appending. The `set()` method always replaces the previous diagnostics for the URI:\n\n```typescript\n// Wrong: diagnostics accumulate across runs\ncollection.set(uri, [...collection.get(uri)!, ...newDiags]); // don't do this\n\n// Correct: full replacement\ncollection.set(uri, newDiags);\n```\n\n### Pattern 6: Checking for Diagnostics Before Code Actions\n\nCode action providers often query the collection directly rather than using `getDiagnostics()`, to limit the scope to their own extension's issues:\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/git/src/diagnostics.ts\nprovideCodeActions(document, range): vscode.CodeAction[] {\n    const diagnostics = this.diagnosticsManager.getDiagnostics(document.uri);\n    // diagnosticsManager internally calls: this.diagnostics.get(uri) ?? []\n    return diagnostics\n        .filter(d => d.range.contains(range))\n        .map(d => buildCodeAction(d));\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Disposed Collection Access\n\nAfter calling `dispose()`, all method accesses throw:\n\n```typescript\nconst col = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('test');\ncol.dispose();\n\ncol.name;    // throws: Error: illegal state - object is disposed\ncol.clear(); // throws: Error: illegal state - object is disposed\ncol.set(...) // throws: Error: illegal state - object is disposed\n```\n\n**Mitigation:** Guard collection access with a disposed flag, or ensure `dispose()` is only called during extension deactivation when no further code can access the collection.\n\n### Duplicate Collection Names\n\nIf you call `createDiagnosticCollection('name')` when a collection with that name already exists:\n\n- A warning is logged: `DiagnosticCollection with name 'name' does already exist.`\n- The returned collection has `name === 'name'` (the property is unchanged) but uses a unique internal owner to avoid conflicts.\n- There is **no exception**; the call succeeds silently aside from the log warning.\n\n**Mitigation:** Use unique names per collection, typically matching the extension's display name or a specific feature identifier (e.g., `'typescript'`, `'eslint'`, `'extension-editing'`).\n\n### Diagnostic Limits\n\nVS Code imposes limits on the number of diagnostics to protect editor performance:\n\n- **Per-file limit:** 1,000 diagnostics per URI per collection.\n- **Total limit per collection:** approximately 1,100 diagnostics across all files.\n\nWhen limits are exceeded:\n- Diagnostics are retained in severity order (Error \u2192 Warning \u2192 Information \u2192 Hint).\n- A synthetic `Information`-severity marker is appended: `\"Not showing N further errors and warnings.\"` This marker is visible in the Problems panel but is not accessible via `getDiagnostics()`.\n\n**Mitigation:** For high-volume validators (e.g., parsers that produce many hints), batch and prioritize diagnostics before calling `set()`. Prefer reporting only actionable issues.\n\n### Immutable Return Values\n\nThe array returned by `DiagnosticCollection.get()` is frozen. Attempting to mutate it throws a `TypeError`:\n\n```typescript\nconst diags = collection.get(uri) as vscode.Diagnostic[];\ndiags.push(new vscode.Diagnostic(...)); // TypeError: Cannot add property 2, object is not extensible\ndiags.pop();                            // TypeError: Cannot delete property '1' of [object Array]\ndiags[0] = new vscode.Diagnostic(...); // TypeError: Cannot assign to read only property '0'\n```\n\n**Mitigation:** Always copy the array before modifying: `const copy = [...collection.get(uri)!]`.\n\n### Sparse Diagnostic Arrays\n\nIf you pass a sparse array (with holes) to `set()`, VS Code automatically removes the holes (via `coalesce()`). Only non-null, non-undefined entries are stored:\n\n```typescript\nconst sparse: vscode.Diagnostic[] = new Array(3);\nsparse[1] = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'only this one');\ncollection.set(uri, sparse);\n// collection.get(uri) returns [sparse[1]] \u2014 length 1, no holes\n```\n",

  "content": "# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe VS Code Diagnostic API provides a mechanism for extensions to report code issues \u2014 errors, warnings, informational messages, and hints \u2014 to users within the editor. Diagnostics appear in the Problems panel, as inline squiggles in the editor, and in gutter decorations. They integrate with the code actions system so that extensions can offer quick-fix suggestions alongside reported issues.\n\nDiagnostics are managed through `DiagnosticCollection` objects, which scope a set of diagnostics to a named owner. Multiple collections can report diagnostics for the same file; `vscode.languages.getDiagnostics()` aggregates them all. The API is accessible via the `vscode.languages` namespace.\n\n---\n\n## Core Types\n\n### `Diagnostic`\n\nRepresents a single diagnostic issue scoped to a file and a text range.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport class Diagnostic {\n    range: Range;\n    message: string;\n    severity: DiagnosticSeverity;\n    source?: string;\n    code?: string | number | { value: string | number; target: Uri };\n    relatedInformation?: DiagnosticRelatedInformation[];\n    tags?: DiagnosticTag[];\n\n    constructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity);\n}\n```\n\n#### Constructor\n\n```typescript\nnew Diagnostic(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity)\n```\n\n| Parameter  | Type                | Required | Description                                                                 |\n|------------|---------------------|----------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `range`    | `Range`             | Yes      | The text range to which this diagnostic applies.                            |\n| `message`  | `string`            | Yes      | Human-readable description of the issue.                                    |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity`| No       | Severity level. Defaults to `DiagnosticSeverity.Error` when omitted.        |\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property             | Type                                                                     | Description                                                                                                                        |\n|----------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `range`              | `Range`                                                                  | The editor range to which this diagnostic applies. Must be a valid range within the document.                                     |\n| `message`            | `string`                                                                 | The human-readable message displayed to the user in the Problems panel and in hover tooltips.                                     |\n| `severity`           | `DiagnosticSeverity`                                                     | Controls how the diagnostic is rendered. Defaults to `Error`.                                                                     |\n| `source`             | `string \\| undefined`                                                    | Optional. A human-readable string identifying the source tool, e.g. `'typescript'` or `'eslint'`. Displayed in the Problems panel.|\n| `code`               | `string \\| number \\| { value: string \\| number; target: Uri } \\| undefined` | Optional. A code or identifier for this diagnostic, used by code action providers to match fixes to diagnostics. When the object form is used, `target` is a URI opened when the user clicks \"Learn More\". |\n| `relatedInformation` | `DiagnosticRelatedInformation[] \\| undefined`                            | Optional. Additional context locations for the diagnostic (e.g., duplicate symbol declarations).                                  |\n| `tags`               | `DiagnosticTag[] \\| undefined`                                           | Optional. Metadata tags that alter how the diagnostic is rendered (e.g., fading out unused code).                                 |\n\n#### Behavioral Notes\n\n- `Diagnostic` objects are **value objects** \u2014 they carry no lifecycle of their own and are not disposed.\n- Diagnostics are only valid **within a specific file**; the URI context is provided when publishing via `DiagnosticCollection.set()`.\n- Setting `code` to the object form `{ value, target }` enables a clickable \"Learn More\" link in the Problems panel UI.\n- Sparse arrays passed to `DiagnosticCollection.set()` are automatically compacted \u2014 `null`/`undefined` holes are removed before storage.\n- `Diagnostic` can be subclassed (see usage in tests: `class D2 extends vscode.Diagnostic { customProp = ...; }`), and identity is preserved through code action callbacks.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticCollection`\n\nA container that manages a set of diagnostics scoped to a named owner. Each diagnostic in the collection is associated with a `Uri` (resource identifier).\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticCollection extends Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]> {\n    readonly name: string;\n\n    set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void;\n    set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void;\n\n    delete(uri: Uri): void;\n    clear(): void;\n\n    forEach(\n        callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any,\n        thisArg?: any\n    ): void;\n\n    get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined;\n    has(uri: Uri): boolean;\n    dispose(): void;\n}\n```\n\n#### Lifecycle\n\nInstances are created via `vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection()`. The collection **must be disposed** when no longer needed \u2014 either explicitly by calling `dispose()`, or by registering it in the extension context's `subscriptions` array. Calling `dispose()` implicitly calls `clear()` and removes all associated diagnostics from the UI.\n\nAfter `dispose()` is called, any further method call (including reading `name`) throws `Error: illegal state - object is disposed`.\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property | Type     | Description                                                                                                                                                      |\n|----------|----------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `name`   | `string` | Read-only. The name supplied to `createDiagnosticCollection()`, or an auto-generated name if none was provided. Used as the owner identifier in the Problems panel and by task problem matchers. |\n\n#### Methods\n\n##### `set(uri, diagnostics)`\n\n```typescript\nset(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void\n```\n\nReplaces all diagnostics for the given resource. Passing `undefined` as `diagnostics` removes all diagnostics for that URI (equivalent to calling `delete(uri)`).\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Each call to `set()` fully replaces any previously stored diagnostics for the URI; it does not merge.\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` immediately (before the async propagation to the main thread, which may be debounced).\n- When the number of diagnostics per file exceeds the internal limit (1,000 per file; approximately 1,100 total across all files for a collection), VS Code prioritizes by severity (Errors first, then Warnings, then Information, then Hints) and appends an informational \"Not showing N further errors and warnings\" marker.\n\n##### `set(entries)`\n\n```typescript\nset(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void\n```\n\nBatch-sets diagnostics for multiple resources in a single call.\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Multiple tuples for the same URI are **merged** (concatenated), not replaced. For example, `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` results in `file1` having `[d1, d2]`.\n- A tuple with `undefined` diagnostics (e.g., `[file1, undefined]`) clears all diagnostics accumulated for that URI **up to that point** in the array, but subsequent tuples for the same URI can still add diagnostics.\n- Internally the entries are sorted by URI string before processing to ensure stable merge behavior.\n- Passing `undefined` or a falsy value as the entire `entries` argument clears the collection (equivalent to `clear()`).\n\n##### `delete(uri)`\n\n```typescript\ndelete(uri: Uri): void\n```\n\nRemoves all diagnostics for the given resource. Equivalent to `set(uri, undefined)`.\n\n##### `clear()`\n\n```typescript\nclear(): void\n```\n\nRemoves all diagnostics from the collection for all resources. Does not dispose the collection itself; the collection remains usable after `clear()`.\n\n##### `forEach(callback, thisArg?)`\n\n```typescript\nforEach(\n    callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any,\n    thisArg?: any\n): void\n```\n\nIterates over each URI/diagnostics entry in the collection. Only URIs that currently have diagnostics (i.e., have been set and not subsequently cleared) are visited.\n\n##### `get(uri)`\n\n```typescript\nget(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined\n```\n\nReturns an **immutable, frozen copy** of the diagnostics for the given resource, or an empty array if the resource has no diagnostics in this collection. The returned array cannot be mutated (attempts to push, pop, or replace elements throw a `TypeError`).\n\n**Note:** Returns an empty array (not `undefined`) when the URI is not present in the collection.\n\n##### `has(uri)`\n\n```typescript\nhas(uri: Uri): boolean\n```\n\nReturns `true` if this collection has any diagnostics for the given resource. A URI is considered \"present\" as long as it has been `set()` with a non-undefined, non-empty array and has not been subsequently deleted or cleared.\n\n##### `dispose()`\n\n```typescript\ndispose(): void\n```\n\nFrees all resources and clears all diagnostics. After disposal, all method calls throw. Calling `dispose()` multiple times is safe (subsequent calls are no-ops).\n\n#### Iteration\n\n`DiagnosticCollection` implements `Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]>`, allowing use in `for...of` loops:\n\n```typescript\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n    // process each uri/diagnostics pair\n}\n```\n\n#### URI Case Sensitivity\n\nThe collection respects the case sensitivity of the file system as reported by the VS Code file system info service. On case-insensitive file systems (e.g., Windows), `get()`, `has()`, and `forEach()` treat URIs with different casing as equal.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticSeverity`\n\nEnum controlling how a diagnostic is rendered in the editor and Problems panel.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticSeverity {\n    Error       = 0,\n    Warning     = 1,\n    Information = 2,\n    Hint        = 3\n}\n```\n\n| Member        | Value | Rendering                                                                                          |\n|---------------|-------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `Error`       | `0`   | Red squiggle underline; displayed in the Problems panel with an error icon. Highest priority when diagnostics are truncated due to per-file limits. |\n| `Warning`     | `1`   | Yellow squiggle underline; displayed with a warning icon.                                          |\n| `Information` | `2`   | Blue squiggle underline; displayed with an info icon.                                              |\n| `Hint`        | `3`   | No squiggle by default; displayed as a subtle hint. Lowest priority for truncation purposes.       |\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- `Error` is the default severity when constructing a `Diagnostic` without specifying severity.\n- When diagnostics per file exceed the limit, VS Code retains them in severity order: Errors are preserved first, then Warnings, then Information, then Hints.\n- The TypeScript extension maps TypeScript's `suggestion` category to `Hint`.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticRelatedInformation`\n\nProvides additional location context for a diagnostic, such as pointing to where a duplicate symbol was first declared.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport class DiagnosticRelatedInformation {\n    location: Location;\n    message: string;\n\n    constructor(location: Location, message: string);\n}\n```\n\n#### Constructor\n\n```typescript\nnew DiagnosticRelatedInformation(location: Location, message: string)\n```\n\n| Parameter  | Type       | Required | Description                                                            |\n|------------|------------|----------|------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | Yes      | The source location (URI + range) associated with this related info.   |\n| `message`  | `string`   | Yes      | Human-readable description of why this location is relevant.           |\n\n#### Properties\n\n| Property   | Type       | Description                                                                                         |\n|------------|------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | A `Location` (URI + Range) pointing to the relevant code. May reference a different file entirely.  |\n| `message`  | `string`   | Short description, e.g. `'First declared here'`.                                                    |\n\n#### Behavioral Notes\n\n- Related information is displayed in the Problems panel as sub-entries under the primary diagnostic.\n- Clicking a related information entry navigates to its `location` in the editor.\n- The `location` can point to a **different file** from the primary diagnostic's document.\n- A `Diagnostic` may have multiple `relatedInformation` entries (stored in an array).\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticTag`\n\nEnum providing additional metadata that alters how a diagnostic is visually rendered. Tags do not affect the severity or sort order.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticTag {\n    Unnecessary = 1,\n    Deprecated  = 2,\n}\n```\n\n| Member        | Value | Rendering Effect                                                                                                                                                                                                            |\n|---------------|-------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `Unnecessary` | `1`   | Renders the affected code **faded out**. The degree of fading is controlled by the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\"` theme color. In high-contrast themes, `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.border\"` is used for an underline instead. |\n| `Deprecated`  | `2`   | Renders the affected code with a **strikethrough**.                                                                                                                                                                         |\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Tags are stored in the `Diagnostic.tags` array. A diagnostic may have multiple tags simultaneously.\n- Diagnostics with `Unnecessary` or `Deprecated` tags are still shown in the Problems panel (they are not suppressed), but may be filtered/styled differently by extensions querying diagnostics.\n- Setting `tags` to an empty array (`[]`) or `undefined` has the same effect \u2014 no special rendering.\n\n---\n\n### `DiagnosticChangeEvent`\n\nThe event object emitted by `onDidChangeDiagnostics`.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticChangeEvent {\n    readonly uris: readonly Uri[];\n}\n```\n\n| Property | Type              | Description                                                                        |\n|----------|-------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `uris`   | `readonly Uri[]`  | The list of resource URIs for which diagnostics have changed (added or removed).   |\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- The `uris` array is **deduplicated** across simultaneous changes from multiple collections affecting the same resource.\n- The array is frozen and must not be mutated.\n\n---\n\n## Functions\n\n### `createDiagnosticCollection()`\n\nFactory function that creates a new `DiagnosticCollection`.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection;\n```\n\n**Location:** `vscode.languages` namespace.\n\n#### Parameters\n\n| Parameter | Type     | Required | Description                                                                                  |\n|-----------|----------|----------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `name`    | `string` | No       | The name for the collection. Used as owner identifier in the Problems panel and by task problem matchers. |\n\n#### Return Value\n\nA new `DiagnosticCollection` instance. The caller is responsible for disposing it.\n\n#### Behavioral Notes\n\n- If `name` is omitted or `undefined`, an auto-generated internal name is assigned (e.g., `_generated_diagnostic_collection_name_#0`). This name still appears in the Problems panel but is not human-friendly.\n- If a collection with the given `name` **already exists**, VS Code logs a warning and creates a new collection with a unique, suffixed owner identifier (e.g., `'myext0'`, `'myext1'`). The `name` property on the returned collection still returns the original name, but the internal `owner` used for deduplication is unique.\n- Each collection is independent; diagnostics from different collections are additive. `getDiagnostics(uri)` returns the union of diagnostics from all collections for a URI.\n- The returned collection must be disposed. The standard pattern is to add it to `context.subscriptions` during extension activation.\n\n---\n\n### `getDiagnostics()`\n\nRetrieves diagnostics from all collections across all extensions.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\n// Overload 1: get diagnostics for a specific resource\nexport function getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[];\n\n// Overload 2: get all diagnostics for all resources\nexport function getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][];\n```\n\n**Location:** `vscode.languages` namespace.\n\n#### Overload 1: `getDiagnostics(resource)`\n\n```typescript\ngetDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n```\n\n| Parameter  | Type  | Required | Description                                 |\n|------------|-------|----------|---------------------------------------------|\n| `resource` | `Uri` | Yes      | The URI of the resource to query.           |\n\n**Returns:** An array of `Diagnostic` objects for the given URI, aggregated across **all** `DiagnosticCollection` instances from all extensions. Returns an empty array if no diagnostics exist for the URI.\n\n#### Overload 2: `getDiagnostics()`\n\n```typescript\ngetDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n```\n\n**Returns:** An array of `[Uri, Diagnostic[]]` tuples, one per resource that has at least one diagnostic, aggregated across all collections. Returns an empty array if no diagnostics exist anywhere.\n\n#### Behavioral Notes\n\n- `getDiagnostics()` aggregates diagnostics across **all** registered `DiagnosticCollection` instances, including those from other extensions and those created by VS Code's own built-in features (e.g., task problem matchers, which are exposed via a mirror collection).\n- Diagnostics from task problem matchers are visible via `getDiagnostics()` but are managed by VS Code internally and cannot be modified by extensions.\n- The function respects file-system case sensitivity when matching URIs.\n- The returned arrays are **mutable** (unlike the arrays returned by `DiagnosticCollection.get()`).\n- Changes are not automatically reflected: each call returns a snapshot at the time of invocation.\n\n---\n\n## Events\n\n### `onDidChangeDiagnostics`\n\nAn event that fires whenever the global set of diagnostics changes.\n\n**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):\n\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>;\n```\n\n**Location:** `vscode.languages` namespace.\n\n#### Event Type\n\n`Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>` \u2014 subscribers receive a `DiagnosticChangeEvent` with the list of affected URIs.\n\n#### When It Fires\n\nThe event fires whenever diagnostics are added, replaced, or removed for any resource. This includes:\n\n- Calls to `DiagnosticCollection.set()` (single URI or batch)\n- Calls to `DiagnosticCollection.delete()`\n- Calls to `DiagnosticCollection.clear()`\n- Calls to `DiagnosticCollection.dispose()` (fires for all URIs in the collection)\n- Changes to diagnostics produced by task problem matchers (via the internal mirror collection)\n\n#### Behavioral Notes\n\n- The event is **debounced** with a 50ms delay internally. Multiple rapid changes (e.g., calling `set()` in a loop) are coalesced into a single event emission. The `uris` array in the emitted event contains the **union** of all URIs affected during the debounce window.\n- The `uris` array in `DiagnosticChangeEvent` may contain URIs for which diagnostics were **added**, **changed**, or **removed**. To determine the current state, call `getDiagnostics(uri)` after receiving the event.\n- The event does **not** distinguish between additions and removals; it only signals that something changed for those URIs.\n- Subscribing to this event is the correct mechanism for reacting to diagnostics changes from other extensions.\n\n#### Subscription Pattern\n\n```typescript\nconst disposable = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics((e: vscode.DiagnosticChangeEvent) => {\n    for (const uri of e.uris) {\n        const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n        // react to updated diagnostics\n    }\n});\ncontext.subscriptions.push(disposable);\n```\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Example: Linting a Document\n\nA minimal extension that validates documents and reports errors:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    // Create a named collection; add to subscriptions for automatic disposal\n    const diagnosticCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\n    context.subscriptions.push(diagnosticCollection);\n\n    // Validate on open and on save\n    context.subscriptions.push(\n        vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(validate),\n        vscode.workspace.onDidSaveTextDocument(validate),\n        vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(doc => {\n            // Clean up diagnostics when the file is closed\n            diagnosticCollection.delete(doc.uri);\n        })\n    );\n\n    // Validate documents already open when the extension activates\n    vscode.workspace.textDocuments.forEach(validate);\n\n    function validate(document: vscode.TextDocument): void {\n        if (document.languageId !== 'typescript') {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n        for (let i = 0; i < document.lineCount; i++) {\n            const line = document.lineAt(i);\n\n            if (line.text.includes('TODO')) {\n                const range = new vscode.Range(i, 0, i, line.text.length);\n                const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                    range,\n                    'TODO comment found',\n                    vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n                );\n                diagnostic.source = 'my-linter';\n                diagnostic.code = 'todo-comment';\n                diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Replaces all previous diagnostics for this document\n        diagnosticCollection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n}\n\nexport function deactivate() {}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Tags, Related Information, and Code-Linked Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('advanced-linter');\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n    // Diagnostic with Deprecated tag (strikethrough rendering)\n    const deprecatedDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        new vscode.Range(5, 0, 5, 20),\n        'This API is deprecated. Use newApi() instead.',\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n    );\n    deprecatedDiag.source = 'advanced-linter';\n    deprecatedDiag.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Deprecated];\n    // Link to documentation\n    deprecatedDiag.code = {\n        value: 'DEP001',\n        target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://example.com/migration-guide')\n    };\n\n    // Diagnostic with Unnecessary tag (faded rendering)\n    const unusedDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        new vscode.Range(10, 0, 10, 15),\n        \"'foo' is declared but never used.\",\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Hint\n    );\n    unusedDiag.source = 'advanced-linter';\n    unusedDiag.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n    unusedDiag.code = 'no-unused-vars';\n\n    // Diagnostic with related information pointing to another location\n    const dupDiag = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n        new vscode.Range(20, 0, 20, 10),\n        \"Duplicate symbol 'MyClass'.\",\n        vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n    );\n vscode.Range(5, 0, 5, 10)\n            ),\n            'First declared here'\n        )\n    ];\n\n    const fileUri = vscode.Uri.file('/workspace/src/main.ts');\n    collection.set(fileUri, [deprecatedDiag, unusedDiag, dupDiag]);\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Batch Updates and Event Subscription\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('batch-example');\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n    const file1 = vscode.Uri.file('/workspace/src/a.ts');\n    const file2 = vscode.Uri.file('/workspace/src/b.ts');\n    const file3 = vscode.Uri.file('/workspace/src/c.ts');\n\n    // Batch-set diagnostics for multiple files atomically\n    collection.set([\n        [file1, [new vscode.Diagnostic(new vscode.Range(0, 0, 0, 5), 'Error in a.ts')]],\n        [file2, [new vscode.Diagnostic(new vscode.Range(3, 0, 3, 10), 'Warning in b.ts', vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning)]],\n        [file3, undefined],  // Clears diagnostics for file3 up to this point in the array\n    ]);\n\n    // Iterate over all entries in the collection\n    collection.forEach((uri, diagnostics) => {\n        console.log(`${uri.fsPath}: ${diagnostics.length} diagnostic(s)`);\n    });\n\n    // Or use for...of\n    for (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n        console.log(uri.toString(), diagnostics.length);\n    }\n\n    // React to global diagnostic changes (from any extension)\n    const changeDisposable = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics((e) => {\n        for (const uri of e.uris) {\n            const allDiags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n            console.log(`${uri.fsPath} now has ${allDiags.length} total diagnostic(s)`);\n        }\n    });\n    context.subscriptions.push(changeDisposable);\n\n    // Query all diagnostics across the workspace\n    const allTuples = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\n    for (const [uri, diags] of allTuples) {\n        const errors = diags.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error);\n        console.log(`${uri.fsPath}: ${errors.length} error(s)`);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Real-World Pattern: Diagnostics with Code Actions (from `extensions/git`)\n\nThe Git extension creates a diagnostic collection without a name and hooks it to document changes:\n\n```typescript\nimport { CodeAction, CodeActionKind, Diagnostic, DiagnosticCollection,\n         DiagnosticSeverity, Range, languages, workspace } from 'vscode';\n\nclass CommitMessageValidator {\n    private readonly diagnostics: DiagnosticCollection;\n\n    constructor() {\n        // No name \u2014 auto-generated owner
