= 'line_length';\n                issues.push(d);\n            }\n        }\n\n        this.diagnostics.set(document.uri, issues);\n    }\n\n    getDiagnostics(uri: vscode.Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] {\n        return this.diagnostics.get(uri) ?? [];\n    }\n\n    dispose(): void {\n        this.diagnostics.dispose(); // implicitly calls clear()\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Extension Activation with Context Subscriptions\n\nThe most common pattern is to create the collection during activation and register it for automatic cleanup:\n\n```typescript\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-tool');\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n    // collection.dispose() is called automatically when the extension is deactivated\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Clearing Diagnostics on Document Close\n\nPrevent stale diagnostics for closed files by cleaning up in the `onDidCloseTextDocument` handler:\n\n```typescript\nvscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(doc => {\n    collection.delete(doc.uri);\n}, null, context.subscriptions);\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Registering Collections with `Disposable`\n\nIn classes that manage their own lifecycle, use `_register()` or store in a `Disposable` array:\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/typescript-language-features\nthis._currentDiagnostics = this._register(\n    vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection(owner)\n);\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: Using `set(uri, undefined)` vs `delete(uri)`\n\nBoth are equivalent. Prefer `delete(uri)` for readability when the intent is removal:\n\n```typescript\n// These are equivalent:\ncollection.set(uri, undefined);\ncollection.delete(uri);\n```\n\n### Pattern 5: Avoiding Stale Diagnostics During Revalidation\n\nWhen re-running validation, always call `set()` with the complete new list rather than appending. The `set()` method always replaces the previous diagnostics for the URI:\n\n```typescript\n// Wrong: diagnostics accumulate across runs\ncollection.set(uri, [...collection.get(uri)!, ...newDiags]); // don't do this\n\n// Correct: full replacement\ncollection.set(uri, newDiags);\n```\n\n### Pattern 6: Checking for Diagnostics Before Code Actions\n\nCode action providers often query the collection directly rather than using `getDiagnostics()`, to limit the scope to their own extension's issues:\n\n```typescript\n// From extensions/git/src/diagnostics.ts\nprovideCodeActions(document, range): vscode.CodeAction[] {\n    const diagnostics = this.diagnosticsManager.getDiagnostics(document.uri);\n    // diagnosticsManager internally calls: this.diagnostics.get(uri) ?? []\n    return diagnostics\n        .filter(d => d.range.contains(range))\n        .map(d => buildCodeAction(d));\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Disposed Collection Access\n\nAfter calling `dispose()`, all method accesses throw:\n\n```typescript\nconst col = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('test');\ncol.dispose();\n\ncol.name;    // throws: Error: illegal state - object is disposed\ncol.clear(); // throws: Error: illegal state - object is disposed\ncol.set(...) // throws: Error: illegal state - object is disposed\n```\n\n**Mitigation:** Guard collection access with a disposed flag, or ensure `dispose()` is only called during extension deactivation when no further code can access the collection.\n\n### Duplicate Collection Names\n\nIf you call `createDiagnosticCollection('name')` when a collection with that name already exists:\n\n- A warning is logged: `DiagnosticCollection with name 'name' does already exist.`\n- The returned collection has `name === 'name'` (the property is unchanged) but uses a unique internal owner to avoid conflicts.\n- There is **no exception**; the call succeeds silently aside from the log warning.\n\n**Mitigation:** Use unique names per collection, typically matching the extension's display name or a specific feature identifier (e.g., `'typescript'`, `'eslint'`, `'extension-editing'`).\n\n### Diagnostic Limits\n\nVS Code imposes limits on the number of diagnostics to protect editor performance:\n\n- **Per-file limit:** 1,000 diagnostics per URI per collection.\n- **Total limit per collection:** approximately 1,100 diagnostics across all files.\n\nWhen limits are exceeded:\n- Diagnostics are retained in severity order (Error \u2192 Warning \u2192 Information \u2192 Hint).\n- A synthetic `Information`-severity marker is appended: `\"Not showing N further errors and warnings.\"` This marker is visible in the Problems panel but is not accessible via `getDiagnostics()`.\n\n**Mitigation:** For high-volume validators (e.g., parsers that produce many hints), batch and prioritize diagnostics before calling `set()`. Prefer reporting only actionable issues.\n\n### Immutable Return Values\n\nThe array returned by `DiagnosticCollection.get()` is frozen. Attempting to mutate it throws a `TypeError`:\n\n```typescript\nconst diags = collection.get(uri) as vscode.Diagnostic[];\ndiags.push(new vscode.Diagnostic(...)); // TypeError: Cannot add property 2, object is not extensible\ndiags.pop();                            // TypeError: Cannot delete property '1' of [object Array]\ndiags[0] = new vscode.Diagnostic(...); // TypeError: Cannot assign to read only property '0'\n```\n\n**Mitigation:** Always copy the array before modifying: `const copy = [...collection.get(uri)!]`.\n\n### Sparse Diagnostic Arrays\n\nIf you pass a sparse array (with holes) to `set()`, VS Code automatically removes the holes (via `coalesce()`). Only non-null, non-undefined entries are stored:\n\n```typescript\nconst sparse: vscode.Diagnostic[] = new Array(3);\nsparse[1] = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'only this one');\ncollection.set(uri, sparse);\n// collection.get(uri) returns [sparse[1]] \u2014 length 1, no holes\n```\n",

# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference

## Overview

The VS Code Diagnostic API provides a mechanism for extensions to report code issues — errors, warnings, informational messages, and hints — to users within the editor. Diagnostics appear in the Problems panel, as inline squiggles in the editor, and in gutter decorations. They integrate with the code actions system so that extensions can offer quick-fix suggestions alongside reported issues.

Diagnostics are managed through `DiagnosticCollection` objects, which scope a set of diagnostics to a named owner. Multiple collections can report diagnostics for the same file; `vscode.languages.getDiagnostics()` aggregates them all. The API is accessible via the `vscode.languages` namespace.

---

## Core Types

### `Diagnostic`

Represents a single diagnostic issue scoped to a file and a text range.

**Declaration** (from `src/vscode-dts/vscode.d.ts`):

```typescript
export class Diagnostic {
    range: Range;
    message: string;
    severity: DiagnosticSeverity;
    source?: string;
    code?: string | number | { value: string | number; target: Uri };
    relatedInformation?: DiagnosticRelatedInformation[];
    tags?: DiagnosticTag[];

    constructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity);
}
```

#### Constructor

```typescript
new Diagnostic(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity)
```

| Parameter  | Type                | Required | Description                                                                 |
|------------|---------------------|----------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| `range`    | `Range`             | Yes      | The text range to which this diagnostic applies.                            |
| `message`  | `string`   
... (truncated)
